text:
I LOVE this recipe. I make wedding cakes from my home and this is one of my go to recipes. It's a great base recipe that I use adding flavorings and extracts. The most popular one so far is the original recipe, but with vanilla bean along with the almond, and then raspberry preserves whipped with buttercream filling. I also throw in lemon zest and juice (omitting the almond) and orange zest and juice with a honey simple syrup brushed on the baked and cooled cake. This is my favorite cake recipe, great texture, crumb, very moist, but holds up when handling it to make larger wedding cakes. And holds Marshmallow Fondant (found on this site) beautifully. Thank you so so so much for sharing with us!!
 *** Just an update.*** I know several people wonder if this can adapted to a choc cake. I have done this several times now. Here's what I do: I use Duncan Hines Dark Choc Fudge. Instead of 1c flour i use 2/3c flour and 1/3 cocoa powder. I use Ghirardelli. It comes out wonderful. Hope this helps !

text:
This is a GREAT cake that originates from  Rebecca Sutterby and as short is called the WASC. I recommend it to all. You can easily change  out the white cake mix and almond flavoring and flavor it to your liking (Lemon cake mix w/ vanilla flavoring.. etc.). I also use flavored coffee creamer (liquid version) opposed to water and sometimes yogurt instead of sour cream (in coordinating flavor). I also add 1/2 a packet of pudding mix to make it super moist(instant, dry). Also it does NOT matter if the cake mix already 'has pudding' in it. That is simply a marketing technique. I prefer BC white cake mix, but yellow I prefer DH. Make sure you sift both. The resulting cake will be pretty dense (and SUPER MOIST) in comparison to a typical box cake(it's supposed to be a hybrid scratch cake)and sturdy enough to hold fondant. If you are carving the cake, omit the pudding packet.

text:
This is an absolute keeper. The best white moist cake I have ever tasted. I used a whipped icing and filled layers with pineapple. .I am thinking the next one should have strawberry layers, then trying a lemon  cake mix with pineapple the next time. I made this in 3 round cake layers and it took about 38 minutes to bake. So good, don't look any further. This is better than the most expensive cakes I have had at weddings. The secret to a light cake is to mix as directed but add the whipped egg whites to the batter the last minute not with the other ingredients, otherwise, you will have a denser cake, not a light one. Absolutely worthwhile. Been baking over 38 years and this is the best white cake.

This cake is perfection!  I have made a lot of cakes and this one really hits the spot.  You must try this to believe how good it is.  I made this for my husband's 30th birthday party and everyone loved it.  This is way better than some of the cakes I've ordered from bakeries.  Definitely try this and follow exactly, I wouldn't add anything. I think a 9x13 would be fine also.  thank you CUPYCAKESMURF!

text:
The baking time listed is not accurate.  Pretty much any size cake (even a little 6" round) will take a minimum of 45 minutes.  Most pan sizes will take roughly 1 hour.  Watch for a tiny hairline crack around the edge where the cake has just begun to release from the pan.  In some recipes, that would be "over-done", but the sour cream in this recipe makes the cake shrink slightly more than normal.  The exact moment of center done-ness usually coordinates with the appearance of that hairline crack.  

Also, with the new, smaller 15oz Betty Crocker boxes (not cool, Betty!), you'll need to reduce the water to 1 cup + 2 Tblsp

text:
I did make some changes - I love almond, but I was making this as cupcakes for a group of 1, 2, and 4 year olds, so I left out the almond extract and doubled the vanilla.  I didn't have enough sour cream and used about 2.5 oz of softened cream cheese to make up the difference and get to 1 cup.  Also,  I added about 1 cup of melted semisweet chocolate to 3 cups of the batter, and spooned some of each batter into the liners to make "half and halfs."  I got 24 generously filled cupcakes and one 8" round cake.  I remember hoping that they were worth all the effort. Wow - they are AMAZING.  I am definitely a frosting fan, but I could fully enjoy this cake with nothing on it at all. It's perfectly sweet, very moist, somehow dense and light at the same time - and the flavor is wonderful. This recipe is definitely in my "go-to" collection now. Absolutely yummy.

text:
Although this recipe has a cake mix base, it's kind of a "from scatch" reicpe.  I've always loved the tenderness of cake mix cakes but I'm also a fan of baking from scratch.  I think this recipe takes the good qualities from the cake mix and combines them with the good flavor of a scratch cake. And this recipe is not nearly as quick to put together as a regular mix cake.  It takes a while to gather all the ingredients - especially separating the 8 eggs (I made double recipe) - but it's worth it.  It really is a spectacular cake.I've been looking for an excellent white cake recipe forever and I think this is it.  It's very white - make sure you use CLEAR vanilla extract and only the egg WHITES. The texture is very tender but not so light and fluffy that you can't easily work with the layers.  It's rather sturdy.  It's just moist enough.  It's certainly not dry at all but it's not so moist that it's sticky at all.  Some reviewers claimed that it was crumbly - mine was so far from that. Not crumbly at all.  To ensure even baking, I used my baking strips on each of my cake pans AND I baked them on a double layer of baking sheets.  I doubled the recipe and it made four 9 inch pans - pretty thick layers.  I did not want such a strong almond flavor so I used more vanilla and less almond.  The 2nd time I used cake flour instead of AP. I prefer the cake flour, it made it incredibly tender.  It's excellent. Be sure to use a cake mix with NO added pudding. Like Duncan Hines White.

text:
I very nearly talked myself out of this cake and I'm so glad I didn't.  I planned on making a 3-layer checkerboard cake and wanted something that would hold up to fondant decorations.  This will now be my go-to recipe for vanilla birthday cakes.  While I followed the ingredients exactly & followed other reviewer recommendation to use Betty Crocker as the cake mix (I don't normally use box mixes), I noted that the cake mix has been reduced from 18.25 ounces to 16.25.  Since I was doubling the recipe, I bought an extra box & measured out 4 extra ounces to make up the difference.  I baked this in buttered and floured 9" pans and while my oven is pretty accurate, it took around 35" to bake.  It's worth checking as you near the cook time since oven temperatures vary.  I used room temperature eggs, etc, and baking strips gave me a perfect moist, dense cake with an excellent crumb.  Also, I did reduce the almond flavor by half and increased the vanilla by half.  The 20 or so people at the birthday party couldn't say enough about the cake.  It was WONDERFUL!  Thank you for an excellent recipe. (Since I made this a checkerboard cake, I'm posting a picture.  Check it out!)

I made a 4 tier wedding cake with this recipe using Duncan Hines 16.5 oz white cake mix (4 boxes).  I froze the layers 3 days prior; heavily wrapped in plastic wrap, then foil. This is the first wedding cake I've made and will never use another recipe. It's a major ego-booster :)

This is the BEST CAKE I have ever made.  And I love to make cake.  I only made a couple changes based on others comments.  I doubled the extracts, I also added half a package of vanilla pudding.  I baked in 2 9" round pans.  I layered the cake with a raspberry filling in between the two layers. I made this cake as written and it was very good. It had a very nice texture-it was moist and somewhat dense while still being light and fluffy. Still working on the ratio of vanilla/almond extract, because as written the almond flavor is a little strong to me. However, the true appeal of this recipe is its flexibility. I used a chocolate cake mix, added instant coffee to the water, and used 2/3c flour and 1/3c cocoa (all vanilla, no almond). This produced the best chocolate cupcakes I have ever had. Perfect texture, excellent flavor. Better than all of the completely from scratch chocolate cakes I have made. Definitely a keeper.

text:
I searched for the perfect cake recipe for a long time and this it!  My tips....first, use Pillsbury cake mix.  I've found that the texture is off with other brands.  Second, make sure you line the bottom of your pan with parchment paper.  Also, my personal preference is light colored, heavy aluminum pans.  Also, if you want to try something a little different...I've made with cake 1 and 1/3 cups of crushed oreo cookies & crushed sprinkles on top of the icing.  Just omit the almond extract.  It's AMAZING.  And my favorite buttercream icing recipe with this cake has 3/4 c butter (1 and a half sticks), 1/4 cup crisco, 1 tablespoon of meringue powder (in the cake section at Walmart or Hobby Lobby), 2 teaspoons vanilla extract, 4 tablespoons of half & half,  (optional - 1/4 teaspoon almond extract)...mix together then add 4 cups of powdered sugar.  Done right, this cake is the best!

text:
I love this recipe it makes such a moist cake that is dense enough for fondant or shaping, freezes well without losing flavour or moisture, makes awesome cupcakes as well, 30 from 1 batch. 
I omit the salt, omit the almond extract and double the vanilla and use whole eggs for the egg whites. 
For a chocolate version I substitute half the sugar with cocoa, for lemon I substitute 1/4 the water for lemon juice, for orange(creamsicle) substitute 1/2 the water for orange juice concentrate, for cappuccino I add 1 tbsp instant coffee and substitute the water with coffee, frosted with Rick's Special Buttercream and dust with cocoa and cinnamon.
Everyone raves about this recipe!
The baking time is off in the recipe, usually my cakes take about 35 minutes, cupcakes around 22 minutes.

I'm still scratching my head on this one.  Everything was done properly and the cake turned out, but it tasted just like a box cake, so in my opinion, why bother going through more work and ingredients to get the same type of result?  Couple tips for people who want to make this recipe:    1) I used two round pans (9") and it required 35 minutes in the oven.    2)  Watch out on your cake mix boxes as the brands are now shrinking their cake mix sizes!!   3)  I didn't really notice the almond taste, so if you want it, I would up the amount.  Bottom line is that this was okay, but I would have been just as happy if I stopped at the box mix.

It did a little but that's understandable considering the base is a boxed cake.  With that said, it is a really, really good cake. The only thing that I found was a bit lacking was that it could have had a little bit more almond taste.  Maybe next time I`ll add another 1/2 tsp more of almond extract.  But I'll make it again for sure.  Thanks for posting.

text:
Fantastic cake. Very moist. A bit more dense than straight box cake mix, but not quite dense enough for carving cakes. I've used it for carving, but only cause I hadn't found a better option yet at that time. The cake's great for stacked wedding cakes though, and cupcakes too. It's a very good white cake base that you can alter with extracts and flavors to your own taste (I like using vanilla, almond and butter flavoring, a little less than 1tsp each). You can even use different flavors of cake mix, like lemon or spice, pretty much every flavor but chocolate (I suggest using a completely different recipe for chocolate cakes). Bake times will vary depending on the size of your pan, so just keep an eye on when it starts to set up and test with a cake tester or tooth pick.

text:
I have a new "favorite" wedding cake recipe!!  This cake is SO moist and SO flavorful.  I just baked a large wedding cake using this recipe and EVERYONE at the wedding was raving about how good & how moist the cake was, including the hostesses at the location.  I used crusting buttercream icing.  For the largest layers, I reduced the oven temp & increased the cooking time.  For a 16" layer, it took a little over 90 minutes to cook through at 300 degrees.  For a full 16" x 2" layer, it took 2 1/2 recipes.  Also, since I was doing so many recipes, I didn't want to separate that many eggs, so I bought the liquid egg whites and used 3/4 cup for each recipe, which worked really good.  As another review stated, if you want a truly white cake, use clear vanilla; otherwise will turn out to be somewhat of a "yellow" cake.  GREAT recipe...highly recommend if you want to serve a cake people will remember!!

I will be trying it with a chocolate cake mix this week as I need a dense cake that will  hold up to fondant.  I will sub out the almond with espresso.  I also learned a trick to get completely even layers right out of the oven that don't need to be trimmed before stacking.  Only spray the very middle of your cake pans, cover with a parchment circle and spray just the middle of that.  No spray or grease on the sides of the pan at all.  Works like a charm every single time for even layers that don't need to be trimmed. This has saved me lots of time in pan prepping and decorating.  Happy baking!

The first time I made this cake, about a year ago, it was fantastic. It was moist, with a fine dense crumb. The last 3 times I've made it, it just do sent come out right. This most recent try I used Duncan Hines white cake mix. I do see on the box it is now 16.25 instead of 18.25. Mb that makes a big difference. This time the texture was completely off. It was not dense, it was semi dry and tasted more like an angel food cake. It also had holes in it throughout. Nothing at all like the first try. So I can see how this cake is getting so many differing reviews. So I will try next attempt with Betty crocker or Pillsbury and adjust liquid to the smaller amt in box mix. Very frustrating, because the 1st time was awesome, and I just can't seem to get same results. I will update this after I have experimented using different brands of cake mixes. Hope I can fix it.

text:
I recently made his cake for my daughter's graduation party, and everyone loved it!  Since I needed to make a sheet cake, I did alter the recipe just a little so it would raise appropriately.  I added a teaspoon of baking soda into the sour cream, and let it expand a bit, then just gently folded in the baking soda-sour cream mixture last, after all other ingredients were mixed.  I also added one extra teaspoon of vanilla and eliminated the almond extract.  This cake was super moist and delicious! I frosted it with a simple whipped butter cream frosting smoothed flat so that I could decorate it.

text:
I am only giving this recipe 4 stars as i have made this 2 different ways now. The first time i made it as cupcakes for my daughters birthday snack at school and it turned out good. The 2nd time i made a few changes. I used confetti cake mix and added half a pkg of vanilla pudding mix (instant) and also added 1 cup of white chocolate chips.  I was making a double layer cake so i placed in 2 round cake pans and baked until light golden brown on top (about 30 min).  The results were AMAZING!!!  I used a cream cheese frosting and it went great with the cake (although i could have eaten it without the frosting). I made the double layer cake for my daughters birthday party and she loved it, in fact everybody loved it.  The few changes really made it a cake to remember.

text:
Awesome flavor!  I doubled the recipe to make a 10" square and 8" square layered cake.  Used fat-free sour cream and half Splenda for the sugar.  This held up wonderfully when cutting into layers.  I baked the cakes together and removed the 8" at 55 minutes and continued baking the 10" for a total 70 minutes.  The 8" was perfect, the 10" was slightly over baked.  Since this was a practice run for a wedding cake, I tried three different fillings from this site: Chocolate Fudge Buttercream Frosting  (super, but so overwhelming that the almond flavor didn't come through), Special Buttercream Frosting (using Almond extract), and one made of raspberries.  All tasty, but enjoyed raspberry best and I am always a chocolate/caramel girl before fruit flavors any day!  The crowd had pretty even reviews and all were enjoyed.  We covered the cakes with the Marshmallow Fondant  recipe on this site and once we got the hang of it, it went well!

text:
This cake does NOT respond well to movement while baking.  It will fall/crater if you move it too much before it is cooked through!  It also takes a LOT longer than 25 minutes to cook in every pan I used.  In the oval pan set I used, which are all 2 deep, the 6 took about 40 minutes to cook.  The large one, which is 16, took about 1 hour 40 minutes to cook.  This is a very dense, moist cake and tastes great, though!  I also made it with chocolate cake mix.  I did not add the almond extract on either kind, as Im not big on almond and my hubby is allergic.  On the white cake, I added 1/8 tsp of cheesecake candy flavoring instead of the almond extract.  On the chocolate cake, I just used 1 tsp of butter flavor in place of the almond extract.  I think that caramel or irish crme flavoring would also work well.

text:
Made this with Duncan Hines white cake, used cake flour instead of all-purpose, and added 1/4 cup additional cake flour to make up for the difference between the boxed mix and actual recipe. I also skipped the almond extract and doubled the vanilla, and used 3 while eggs instead of whites. 

As for technique, I mixed all the wet ingredients together, sifted the dry ingredients in a separate container and alternated additions in 3 batches and mixed with a hand mixer. 

I divided the batter equally by weight into two 8 inch cake rounds that are 3" high (standard height pans are too shallow).  Baked them for 45 min total-- perfect timing.

Crumb is nice. Dense,  but not gummy. Lighter than a pound cake. Did NOT taste like boxed mix. 

All in all, very happy with this recipe and will definitely use it again!!

text:
This cake is AMAZING! I've been searching and searching for a white/vanilla/non-chocolate cake recipe to make a rainbow cake for my kids' birthday party.  After three recipes, I didn't need to search any further!

I made three batches of this recipe, so I could have 6 layers for my cake.  Here are the changes I made: Because the white cake mix is now 16.25oz., I added 2 oz. of flour to the recipe.  Also, as it didn't matter that the layers weren't pure white, I did 3 eggs instead of 4 egg whites. And lastly, someone dipped in to my sour cream (and I didn't have enough), so I added about an extra tablespoon of non-fat vanilla yogurt to make up the difference.  I wanted vanilla flavor only, so doubled the vanilla and omitted the almond. The cakes baked for 35 minutes (two-9" layers at a time) in a light-colored cake pan.

The taste is absolutely perfect for what I wanted.  Everyone was gobbling up the tops that I cut off (to flatten my layers).  I had to freeze the layers as the party is a week away, but this will make it easier to frost anyhow.  So excited!  Thanks for a great recipe!

After a disaster day of baking using a different recipe, I decided to take a chance on this one.  Using whole eggs instead of whites and 2 teaspoons of vanilla (in place of vanilla and almond) this cake turned out perfectly!  Using whole eggs instead of whites meant tt was sturdy enough to stack 2 feet high. (I probably used 3 eggs in place of 4 whites.)  The cake was moist, didn't crumb too much, and super flavorful.  Everyone is surprised when I tell them that a box mix is one of the ingredients.  The other additions give this cake a gourmet flavor, while the box mix ensures the texture people expect.

This was an excellent cake.  I made it for a coworker's birthday, who was on a diet.  This was already a pretty low calorie cake, but I made it lower yet by using 1/2 c light sour cream and 1/2 cup light applesauce and only 1 tbls oil.  For the topping I used light cool whip mixed with some powdered sugar.  It turned out great, and everyone said it was really good and couldn't believe it was a "light" cake.

Using this cake for a wedding. Baked up beautifully, nice flat layers, denser and easy to ice but still moist and delicious. Found out it actually tastes better when it sits a day or two, in my opinion. I made marble cake and straw filling. Made the choc just the same as the white and swirled together. Two white and one chocolate made enough batter for a 12" sq, a 10" sq and a 6" square perfectly. Did this times 2 for 2 layers. The cake splits well too, will be splitting to make 4 layers with straw in between.

Made these into 24 cupcakes. Seriously - SOOOO GOOOOD! One reviewer said the crumb was too dense for her taste. That put me over the edge to try this recipe. I love a good, dense crumb. I'm not a huge fan of storebought cakes and cakemixes. The crumb of this cake is more like angel food cake than a typical cake. Mmmmmm. The taste is unbeatable! I absolutely love the almond flavoring. Such a delicious taste. I topped this with whipping cream mixed with cream cheese and sugar. Really... these were so delicious. Could work for the nicest of nice situations - including a wedding. Lovely pearly white look. The picture (shown) really doesn't do them justice.

text:
I followed the recipe exactly.  I had super high expectations because I was hoping to find a recipe that tasted just like my oh-so delicious wedding cake, and this wasn't it, but nonetheless, it was still good.  It was moist, the texture was light, but it still had that boxed cake taste, rather than the flavor that the professionals can do.  Even though my oven was exactly at 325, I also had to cook it for an additional 15min because it remained soupy in the middle.  Luckily, the edges didn't burn at all during that extra time, and it came out looking very nice.  Once it cooled, I used a vanilla glaze over the top and covered it with sliced almonds.  Overall, it was very good.

text:
I have made this several times now (mainly for birthdays) and it is ALWAYS a huge hit.  I personally think the baking time of 25 minutes is way too short, even when divided into 9" rounds, I always have to add at least 10 minutes, sometimes 15.  Also, the recipe doesn't call for it, but I whisk the egg whites a bit, otherwise it can come out too dense.  One last recommendation, a "light" frosting is best, the cake is so flavorful and rich, a straight buttercream frosting can be too sweet, using a heavy cream instead of milk or even adding some whipped topping to the frosting can help "cut" the sweetness.  All that being said, this is a GREAT recipe and good as is.

text:
If time is what I was trying to save by using the cake mix for a base, then this wasnt the cake recipe for me! It took me SEVENTY minutes (not a typo) to sift the cake mix. My arms were sore the next day. I need ideas/help with that! Aside from that, here are the other comments about this recipe -  I could taste the 'white box cake mix' flavor. I had hoped that all the other ingredients would have eliminated the 'box cake' flavor.  The texture was stunning (my sifting efforts were rewarded)  I used butter instead of oil.  A comment had said a 9x13 would work fine. Plan on doubling the cook time. I gave it 5 extra minutes. I gave it 10 more. I gave it 10 more. I gave it 7 more. Fifty seven minutes to cook it in a 9x13 airbake pan.  Almond Buttercream Frosting on top. It was too much to have almond flavored frosting on almond-flavored cake. The frosting needed the almond flavor either eliminated or reduced.  Everyone LOVED LOVED LOVED this cake. It was the best cake I've ever made (and my first sort of 'real' one)..but, I will be on the hunt for a recipe for a 'from scratch' wedding cake. The only good reason I can see for using the cake mix is to save time. It did not do that and tasted like box cake. The heaviness of the cake mix made the sifting 'next to' impossible.  I will make this cake again IF I can find a better sifting solution. I couldnt believe how many little hard weird granules are in box cake. That's why I kept at the sifting, in case you were wondering :)

text:
It's been a long time since I've had wedding cake, but this recipe tastes pretty close to how I remember it tasting! I added 1/4 cup of cake flour to make up for the difference in cake sizes now, as recommended by another reviewer (I used a Pilsbury cake mix that was 15.25 ounces). I made this into cupcakes. I filled the cupcake liners 2/3 full, which resulted in nicely domed cupcakes with no over-spill onto the cupcake tins. It made 24 full size cupcakes, 12 mini cupcakes and 5 oval easter egg shaped cakes. I was really happy with the results, and am looking forward of trying this "method" with other flavors of cake mix. Thanks for sharing the recipe!

text:
So to make this better I started with a very good cake mix.  Then I used melted real butter instead of vegetable oil, I also added one tablespoon of butter for each yolk that was not added on top of the amount I used in the place of the oil.  Cakes need fat and removing the yolk makes for a nice white cake but also removes allot of the texture and flavor. I used milk instead of water.  Also spend a little on the extract making sure to use real extract and not something artificial will make a huge difference.  Also real sour cream complete with all the calories is best.  This is one recipe trying to cut calories from will not produce great results.

text:
Excellent cake.  I made two -- the first I made exactly according to the recipe.  The second was a chocolate cake that I made following Tami Baity's advice, substituting 1/3 cup of cocoa for 1/3 cup of the flour.  Both were delicious, moist and sturdy.  I made the white cake in three layers and filled it with a pineapple filling.  The chocolate cake was a two-layer cake filled with raspberry filling.  I got rave reviews for both.  Neither cake tasted like a "box" cake.  This will be the only recipe I use for layer cakes from now on.  Thank you!  **For those complaining of a crumbly cake, I cooled my layers, then wrapped them in plastic wrap and put the layers in freezer ziplock bags and froze them ahead of time.  When I was ready to finish the cakes several days later, I pulled them out of the freezer, filled them and iced them while they were still frozen.  No crumbs, no tearing apart of the cake.  It requires a little planning ahead, but it was SO easy.

This cake was wonderful!  Moist and excellent taste and texture.  I am a non-baker and had no issues with it.  I made it into 2 9" round layers.  They came out completely flat - not always the case for my layer cakes.  They weren't delicate and were good to frost.  I used a cream cheese frosting and it was a great compliment.

I don't have a picture of a slice but you can see from the frosted bit how well it went together and non-lopsided it was.

Made this last week for hubby's stepdad birthday.  Made exactly as written using Pillsbury moist supreme white cake mix which now only comes in 15.25 ounces so added another 3 ounces to equal 18.25. I have made this twice now with different results.  The taste both times has been incredible, but the 2nd time I read more reviews and followed those who indicated to use milk instead of water.  I will go back to water.  It does nothing for the taste, but the texture I found the first time to be far better, more dense, than the 2nd.  It did not cut cleanly.  It did better with a sharper knife but I still felt on some slices I was cutting into the cake. In addition, large air pockets also resulted and that look was not my vision unfortunately.  Good thing it tasted good! :-)

text:
Originally made this recipe as-is for cupcakes (found the recipe on another site)...were gummy because of overfilling cupcake liners and under-cooking. Tried this again as a layer cake with these changes and found the cake simply delicious.
Here are my changes:
Pillsbury's white cake containing pudding (18.25 oz);
(2) 8-inch layers at 325 degrees for approximately 47  minutes;
3 whole eggs instead of 4 egg whites;
I used 1 teaspoon vanilla extract, 1  teaspoons almond extract, and 1 teaspoon of buttery sweet dough emulsion (found at King Arthur flour website);
Used milk instead of water;
Filled inner layer with Smuckers Strawberry Sundae Topping (small amount), then with frosting (copycat of Publix buttercream);
Frosted outside of cake with Publix buttercream...very rich icing.

text:
Good basic almond flavored white cake that adapts well with other flavored varieties.  Note the recipe is for the old 18.5 oz cake mix box and most are now 15.5 oz. and it really requires the extra amount of cake mix to work out well.  Just open another box and add 3 oz and save the balance of it for another cake.  And  trust me...do not use "light"  style sour cream in this recipe.....  that was a true disaster!  Next time I used full sour cream and it turned out great.  I have found that light sour cream deteriorates for some reason in most recipes that I have used it in . Save it for topping a baked potatoe!  Really... if you are making a cake who is concerned about calories?

text:
I take my desserts VERY seriously.  This recipe deserves your serious consideration; it's awesome!  I used a 15.25 oz cake mix and it turned out great!!!  With the smaller size cake mix than recommended, just to make sure it was still moist and dense I added 1 oz of custard powder (assuming 1 oz instant coconut pudding would work, too) and an additional 2 T oil.  I substituted 1 c plain greek yogurt.  As I prefer less sweet European-like desserts, I omitted the extra sugar and didn't miss it one bit.  I split the 2 layers into 4 and brushed the top of each layer with coconut milk (almond milk, regular milk with a bit of extract flavoring or cream would also work perfectly) with a super moist result.  I made it 2 days ahead of time, frosted and stored in the frig.  Absolutely fantastic!!!

country:

text:
I have been using this recipe for several years now and always get rave reviews.  I have adapted it to every flavor you can imagine.  If I don't need a "white" cake, I use any flavor of cake mix and substitute 3 whole eggs for the egg whites. 
 You can substitute coffee, carmelized liquid sugar or fruit juice for the water, pumpkin for the sour cream...the combinations are endless and I've never had a flop!  The problem I now have is that Duncan Hines cake mixes have recently reduced their volume - very frustrating!  The larger mix always made a perfect amount for a 3-layer 9" cake.  Now I have to experiment to figure out what to add to get the volume I need, but I'll get there eventually!  Here is something I've learned about this recipe.  The cake holds up great to frosting and stacking, but it can be very crumbly when cutting and serving.  I now bake, cool, wrap and freeze the layers at least overnight and then I frost, fill and stack them right out of the freezer.  They are much easier to cut and serve if they've been frozen and it doesn't affect the taste at all.

text:
This cake recipe is almost exactly the same as the Almond Wedding cake in the Cake Doctor book.  The one in the book is doubled and requires a tad bit less water.  (I followed hers more closely and used the lesser amount of water.)  Believing you get out what you put in, I used full fat sour cream, Land of Lakes butter, and a Duncan Hines cake mix.  I was very nervous when I realized I failed to notice the discrepancy between the ounces in the recipe and the ounces on my box.  It turned out white, light in texture, not gummy at all.  I personally like the tiny bit of crunch (probably from the sugar) on the very exterior of the cake.  Sadly my daughter will probably cut the dome off when she decorates the cake.  (I bake them, she decorates them.)  Since the client requested almond flavor, I would probably double the almond next time.  All in all, I liked this cake and can't understand what all the fuss is about the mix.

Edited to add:  I contacted Ann Byrne, author of the Cake Doctor books, and asked her about the smaller cake mixes, if my success was a fluke, why some complained about gummy results etc.  She said that for some of her recipes it might not matter.  She has been testing some of her recipes with the smaller mixes.  For those where it did seem to matter more flour might need to be added (up to 6 T) and/or less water might be necessary.  Since her recipe used 1/3 less water, that could be why mine turned out.

My recommendation:  Don't wait until the day you need

text:
Anyone that does not rate this 5 stars is making a mistake when making this.  You can overcook this and it still taste great!  Use a name brand cake mix for the base cake.  Also, note that current cake mixes and NOT the size of this recipe.  I make often so I just weigh it and add in the correct amount the recipe calls for.  I make wedding cakes so I do double it.  People go nuts over this.  You do not need to do a thing to this recipe it is perfect the way it is.  If you don't like almond of course you can just replace with more vanilla!

text:
Add 1 cup of sour cream and 1 package of Hershey's white chocolate instant pudding mix before mixing. I've used this recipe with all different cake mix flavors, as cupcakes, sheet cake, and layer cake. It always comes out rich, dense, and moist! Delicious! Try this for a yummy whipped topping frosting: cream 1 8 oz. package of softened cream cheese with 1 cup milk. Add 1 package of instant Hershey's white chocolate pudding mix. Stir or lightly beat in one large container of Cool Whip topping, (or the equivalent in sweetened whipped cream). It will hold its shape when piped through a pastry bag, tastes delicious, and has a much lower carb count than a sugar based frosting. Really good!

This was exactly what I was after. I used this cake mix to make cupcakes, which I filled with raspberry pie filling, and then frosted with a vanilla-almond buttercream icing. YUM! 

This seems to be a pretty forgiving recipe. My boxed white cake mix was a 16-oz mix (instead of the 18.25 that the recipe called for), and I was short on sour cream. I used probably a little over half the amount called for (it was all I had). I did not adjust any of the other ingredients, even though I was short on those two items, and the cake still turned out wonderfully! I will definitely make it again... and hopefully next time I'll have the right amount of everything!

text:
This was SO good!  I think it's the best cake I've had.  A wedding cake was being made and we needed to make the recipe 4 times for 2- 10" pans, 2- 8" pans, & 2- 6 pans.  We didn't want the almond flavoring so doubled up on the vanilla.  We used the powdered white vanilla (found in the grocery store) which adds excellent flavor to the cake.   If using the powdered white vanilla, it is best to add it to the dry ingredients.    We did have a bit extra cake mix which we baked and shared.  Can't wait to try it with other flavors of cake mix.  It is important to let the cake cool in the pan for 10 minutes before turning out onto a rack to cool and then peel off the parchment paper (if you used it).  Thank you for a great recipe!

No changes to the recipe.  We baked 4 other 'from scratch' white cake recipes as trials for my parents' anniversary cake.  Finally, I decided to use this one. I was concerned that the cake mix was going to 'cheapen' the end product but I was very wrong.  This recipe was perfect for torting and filling (we used raspberry jam and Swiss merengue buttercream) and it held up beautifully without tearing or crumbling. The flavor was very good as well. The sour cream probably behaves like buttermilk in 'scratch' recipes.  One batch made enough to fill a 12 inch layer and  4 inch.  Or  10 and 6.

This is my new go-to white cake recipe. It was delicious-my husband and I ate several with no icing at all and we didn't need it! text:
Wonderful recipe.  I doubled this recipe for a wedding cake because I had a last minute order. I usually bake everytihng from scratch. Here are a few changes I made:
Instead of 2 cups of water, I added 2 cups of buttermilk
Added 1 tsp of baking soda (because the buttermilk and sour cream are very acidic)
I used pasteurized egg whites
Also, I double sifted all of the dry ingredients before adding the wet
The cake turned out moist and delicious and not overly sweet.  It held up to being torted and filled with apricot preserves, frosted meringue buttercream and decorated with buttercream flowers.

I baked this cake this afternoon but like one other person had mentioned I used an 9x13 inch pan & also made 6 cupcakes. I wanted to use a disposable pan since I'm taking the cake somewhere & don't have the larger pan except in my good pans. I did bake both at 350 instead of 325 and the cake took about 35-40 minutes whereas the cupcakes were 30-35 minutes. I used a chocolate frosting recipe and decorated with sliced almonds. My husband & I both thought the cupcakes were really good. He wasn't sure he would like it as well with a white frosting. He even suggested they would be good with whip cream in the middle.

What a life saver!  Great crumb/density, stayed moist, fabulous flavor and better yet... EASY!!!  YUM!!!!  Definitely keeping this one as a standby!

Made some slight changes: 
1) used 1/2 tsp almond extract--which was perfect for me
2) added 1/3 cp sprinkles and made it a funfetti cake!
3) baked in 2 9" rounds for ~35", rotating 1x about 15" into the baking time
4) frosted with a vanilla Swiss Meringue Buttercream

PERFECT!  You wont' be sorry if you give this one a try!

I made this with a chocolate cake mix and instead of the almond extract, just used all vanilla.  This was one of the best cakes I ever made and it was a huge hit with my family.  I would try this with any kind of cake mix because it was dense like a like cake to be and it was super moist.  I baked it in a fluted pan and it took about 37 mins.  To the rater who complained about spending 70 mins sifting the mix...it doesn't say in the instructions to sift it, although I did it myself.  It took me all of 5 mins to sift it using a metal strainer and a plastic scraper.  Glad I did because there are little balls of whatever in there.  Highly recommended.  I'll use the recipe every time now!
